	<header class="entry-header">
		<h1 class="entry-title">Papers</h1>
	</header><!-- .entry-header -->

	<div class="entry-content">
		<ol>
<li>T. Liu, R. Dimpsey, A. Behroozi, and S. Kumaran, <em>Performance Modeling of Business Process Integration Middleware, International Journal of Business Process Integration and Management, to appear 1Q2004.</em></li>
<li>G. Hunt, R. Dimpsey, et. al., Introduction to WebSphere Interchange Server Performance, IBM Red Paper, December 2003.</li>
<li>R. Dimpsey, <em>WebSphere Business Integration Performance, </em>IBM Academy of Technology Best Practices Conference on Performance Engineering, June 2003.</li>
<li>H. Gunther, R. Dimpsey, <em>Something about WebSphere, IBM Academy of Technology Best Practices Conference on Performance Engineering, June 2001.</em></li>
<li>R. Dimpsey, R. Arora, K. Kuiper, <em>IBM Java Virtual Machines, e-business Application Environment Technical Conference, June 2000.</em></li>
<li>R. Dimpsey, R. Arora, K. Kuiper, <em>Java Server Performance: A Case Study of Building Efficient, Scalable JVMs, IBM System&#8217;s Journal, January 2000.</em></li>
<li>S. Baylor, M. Devarkonda, S. Fink, E. Gluzberg, M. Kalantar, P. Muttineni, R. Arora, R. Dimpsey, S. Munroe, <em>Java Server Benchmarks, IBM System&#8217;s Journal</em><strong>, </strong>January 2000.</li>
<li>R. Dimpsey, R. Arora, K. Kuiper, <em>Java Server Performance, </em>IBM Academy of Technology Best Practices Conference on Performance Engineering, September 1999.</li>
<li>S. Baylor, R. Dimpsey, E. Gluzberg, P. Muttineni, <em>Current Performance Issues and Future Directions in Java e-business Middleware, IBM Academy Technology e-Business and Middleware Applications,</em><strong>  </strong>poster session, June 1999.</li>
<li>R. Dimpsey and L. Brissette, <em>WARP Server SMP Performance Features</em>, IBM Personal Systems, April 1997.</li>
<li>R. Dimpsey and R. Iyer, <em>A Measurement-Based Modeling Technique to Predict the Performance Impact of System Modifications, IEEE Transactions on Parallel and Distributed Systems, January 1995.</em></li>
<li>R. Dimpsey, <em>Benchmarking the Scalability of Shared Memory Multiprocessors, Compudata</em><strong>,</strong> 1994.</li>
<li>B. Alexander, R. Dimpsey, and B. Olszewski, <em>The performance of the AIX Operating System on MP, AIXPert, November 1994.</em></li>
<li>R. Dimpsey, <em>SMP Scaling Results</em>, AIXPRESS, September 1993.</li>
<li>R. Iyer and R. Dimpsey, <em>Evaluation of parallel processors, Keynote for IEEE Region 10 International Conference on Computers, Communications, and Automaton, November 1992.</em></li>
<li>R. Dimpsey, <em>Performance Evaluation and Modeling Techniques for Parallel Processors, CRHC Technical Document, UILU-ENG-92-2234, University of Illinois, September 1992.</em></li>
<li>R. Dimpsey and R. Iyer, <em>Predicting the Impact of Scheduling Modifications on System Performance: Case Study, Hawaii International Conference on System Sciences</em><strong>, </strong>January 1992.</li>
<li>R. Dimpsey and R. Iyer, <em>Modeling and Measuring Multiprogramming and System Overheads on a Multiprocessor: Case Study, Journal of Parallel and Distributed Computing</em><strong>, </strong>August 1991.</li>
<li>R. Dimpsey and R. Iyer, <em>Performance Prediction and Tuning on a Multiprocessor, Proc. of International Symposium on Computer Architecture, May 1991.</em></li>
<li>R. Dimpsey and R. Iyer, <em>Performance Degradation due to Multiprogramming and System Overheads in Real Workloads: Case Study on a Shared Memory Multiprocessor, Proc. Int&#8217;l. Conf. on Supercomputers, June 1990.</em></li>
<li>R. Dimpsey and R. Iyer, <em>Multiprogramming Performance Degradation: Case Study, Proc. Int&#8217;l. Conference on Parallel Processing</em><strong>,</strong> August 1989.</li>
<li>R. Dimpsey and R. Iyer, <em>Performance Analysis of a Shared Memory Multiprocessor: Case Study, Proc. Int&#8217;l. Conference on Parallel Processing</em><strong>,</strong> August 1988.</li>
<li>R. Dimpsey, <em>Performance Analysis of the Alliant FX/8 Multiprocessor using Statistical Clustering, </em>CRHC Technical Document, UILU-ENG-88-2255, University of Illinois, June 1986.</li>
</ol>

	<header class="entry-header">
		<h1 class="entry-title">Education</h1>
	</header><!-- .entry-header -->

	<div class="entry-content">
		<p>Ph.D., Electrical Engineering (August 1992), University of Illinois, Urbana- Champaign.</p>
<p><strong>Thesis:</strong><em>  Performance Evaluation and Modeling Techniques for Parallel Processors.</em></p>
<p>M.S., Electrical Engineering (May 1988), University of Illinois, Urbana-Champaign.</p>
<p><strong>Thesis:</strong><em><strong> </strong> Performance Analysis of a shared Memory Multiprocessor: Case Study.</em></p>
<p>B.S., Computer Engineering (May 1986), University of Illinois, Urbana-Champaign.</p>
<p><strong> </strong></p>
			</div><!-- .entry-content -->

	</article><!-- #post-51 -->

<article id="post-44" class="post-44 page type-page status-publish hentry">
	<header class="entry-header">
		<h1 class="entry-title">Software Shipped!</h1>
	</header><!-- .entry-header -->

	<div class="entry-content">
		<div></div>
<div> A key focus of my career has been designing, building and shipping software used at large scale.  Here is a list of shipping products that I contributed to in my 10 years at Microsoft.</div>
<ul>
<li><i>Windows Vista,</i> Nov, 2006.</li>
<li><em>Microsoft .NET Framework 3.0,</em> Nov, 2006.</li>
<li><em>Visual Studio 2008,</em> Nov, 2007.</li>
<li><em>Microsoft .NET Framework 3.5, </em>Nov, 2007.</li>
<li><em>SQL Server 2008,</em> Aug, 2008.</li>
<li><em>Visual Studio 2008 SP1, </em>Aug, 2008.</li>
<li><em>Microsoft .NET 3.5 SP1, </em>Aug, 2008.</li>
<li><em>Silverlight 2,</em> Oct, 2008.</li>
<li><em>BizTalk Server 2009, </em>Mar, 2009.</li>
<li><em>Microsoft Silverlight Version 3,</em> June, 2009.</li>
<li><em>Windows 7, </em>June 2009.</li>
<li><em>Windows Server 2008 R2, July, 2009.</em></li>
<li><em>Visual Studio 2010, </em>Mar, 2010.</li>
<li><em>Microsoft .NET Framework 4.0, </em>Mar, 2010.</li>
<li><em>Microsoft Silverlight Version 4, </em>Apr, 2010.</li>
<li><em>Windows Server AppFabric, </em>Jun, 2010.</li>
<li><em>Visual Studio 2010 SP1, Mar, 2011.</em></li>
<li><em>Microsoft Communication Protocols Program, </em>May, 2011.</li>
<li><em>Windows Azure 2012 Release, June 2012.</em></li>
<li><em>Visual Studio 2012</em>, Aug, 2012.</li>
<li><em>Microsoft .NET Framework 4.5</em>, Aug, 2012.</li>
<li><em>Windows Server 2012,</em> Aug, 2012.</li>
<li><em>Service Bus for Windows Server, Oct, 2012.</em></li>
<li><em>Workflow Manager for Windows Server, Oct, 2012.</em></li>
<li><i><em>Windows Azure Services for Windows Server, </em>Dec, 2012.</i></li>
</ul>
<div></div>
<p>I have also worked, in multiple roles, on many cloud-based services.  These do not &#8220;ship&#8221; at a specified time but are updated continuously.  These include:</p>
<ul>
<li>Azure Service Bus</li>
<li>Azure Workflows</li>
<li>Azure WebSites</li>
<li>Microsoft Commerce Platform (on-line payment systems)</li>
<li>Supply Chain Cloud-based micro-Services supporting Microsoft Plan, Source, Make, Deliver, Return SCOR functions</li>
</ul>
<div></div>
<p>While at IBM I focused on Systems performance and helped ship multiple versions of AIX, OS/2, Java, and WebSphere.</p>
			</div><!-- .entry-content -->

	</article><!-- #post-44 -->

<article id="post-22" class="post-22 page type-page status-publish hentry">
	<header class="entry-header">
		<h1 class="entry-title">About</h1>
	</header><!-- .entry-header -->

	<div class="entry-content">
		<p>Robert Dimpsey is a senior lecturer in the Computing and Systems Software (CSS) department at the University of Washington Bothell (UWB).  He has taught sections of CSS332, CSS340, CSS342, CSS430, CSS432, CSS490 (Cloud), CSS501 and CSS502.  He is currently teaching Could computing and Applied Algorithmics.</p>
<p>Before joining UWB, Prof. Dimpsey worked in many capacities designing, developing, and shipping  industry leading software for Microsoft and IBM.  He has worked as Director of Development, General Manager, Product Unit Manager, Development Manager, as well as Performance developer.   Products shipped include operating systems, platforms, developer frameworks and tools, and cloud services.</p>
<p>Some highlights of products shipped include:</p>
<ul>
<li>AIX:  IBM&#8217;s industry leading Unix System (worked on kernel level perf.)</li>
<li>Java Virtual Machines for Linux, AIX, and OS/2</li>
<li>OS/2:  IBM&#8217;s long-gone personal computing operating system</li>
<li>Windows Communication Foundation (WCF):  SOAP and RESTful web services framework  (as performance lead, Dev Manager, Product Unit Manager (PUM))</li>
<li>Windows Workflow (WF): a fully declarative language<br />
executing on a persistent runtime (as PUM, GM)</li>
<li>Visual Studio Tooling for WCF and WF, including visual extensible visual designers</li>
<li>Azure Service Bus:  High scale Cloud-based messaging and hybrid relay support for Microsoft&#8217;s cloud Platform</li>
<li>Azure Commerce:  Cloud services processing all of Microsoft&#8217;s on-line transactions (Director of Development, Payments/Billing)</li>
<li>Microsoft Supply Chain Engineering: Cloud services responsible for Plan, Source, Make, Deliver, and Care functions (Advisor / Consultant)</li>
<li>See here <a href="http://faculty.washington.edu/dimpsey/wordpress/software-shipped/">here</a> for a more complete list</li>
</ul>
<p>Prof. Dimpsey has a BS in Computer Engineering and a Masters and PhD in Electrical Engineering from the University of Illinois at Urbana-Champaign.  In addition to teaching at UWB he has taught at the University of Texas Austin as an Adjunct Professor and the University of Illinois at Urbana-Champaign as a Teaching Assistant.</p>
<p>Current areas of interest include computer system performance analysis, and development methodologies and architecture of large cloud-based services.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
			</div><!-- .entry-content -->

	</article><!-- #post-22 -->

<article id="post-11" class="post-11 page type-page status-publish hentry">
	<header class="entry-header">
		<h1 class="entry-title">Welcome!</h1>
	</header><!-- .entry-header -->

	<div class="entry-content">
		<p>&nbsp;</p>
<p><a href="http://faculty.washington.edu/dimpsey/wordpress/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/Bobpic2.jpg"><img class="size-medium wp-image-13 aligncenter" src="http://faculty.washington.edu/dimpsey/wordpress/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/Bobpic2-300x217.jpg" alt="Bobpic2" width="300" height="217" srcset="http://faculty.washington.edu/dimpsey/wordpress/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/Bobpic2-300x217.jpg 300w, http://faculty.washington.edu/dimpsey/wordpress/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/Bobpic2-1024x740.jpg 1024w, http://faculty.washington.edu/dimpsey/wordpress/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/Bobpic2-498x360.jpg 498w, http://faculty.washington.edu/dimpsey/wordpress/wp-content/uploads/2015/09/Bobpic2.jpg 1045w" sizes="(max-width: 300px) 100vw, 300px" /></a></p>
<p>I will be teaching two courses in the Winter 2019 quarter:  Operating Systems (CSS430) and Cloud Computing (CSS490).</p>
<p>Please find details below:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="http://courses.washington.edu/css430/">CSS430:</a>  Operating Systems</li>
</ul>
<p>&nbsp;</p>

<!-- ----------------------- Abstract ------------------------ -->
   <td width="10" height="400" bgcolor="#000099">
   <img src="HK.jpg" nosave="">  
   </td>

   <td height="400" width="463">
   <center>
       <p>
           <b>Course Description</b> <br>
       </p>
   </center>
       This course is a	continuation of CSS 501 and covers advanced data structures 
       including trees, balanced trees, heaps, graphs, and hash tables along with the 
       associated algorithms.  Students learn how to analyze a problem and design and 
       implement a solution using object-oriented design and programming with a focus 
       on inheritance and polymorphism.  Students also study the basic formal notations 
       of languages cover topics such as context free grammars.
   <p>
   </p>

<!-- ----------------------- Abstract ------------------------ -->

<h2><strong>Together we will.<br />
</strong></h2>
<p>UW alumni are passionate. Passionate about possibility, passionate about community and passionate about purple and gold. Sharing a connection across three campuses and extending to places all over the world, UW alumni are united in the belief that together we will make a difference. The UW Alumni Association is proud to support the collective passion of so many who stand up for the University of Washington. Join us.</p>

      <div id='main_content' class="uw-body-copy" tabindex="-1">

        

<p><img src="https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/33/2019/07/16174218/header-parents3b.jpg"></p>
<div>
<div class="container">
<div class="col-md-8">
<h2 class="uni">Welcome #UWFamily</h2>
<p class="intro">Whether you’re a proud Husky alum or new to campus, the department of Parent &amp; Family Programs knows you’ve worked hard to help your student get to college, and we’re honored to welcome you to the UW family.</p>
<p>The path to graduation can be just as challenging for a family as it is for their student. That’s why we’re dedicated to connecting you with the right resources to support your student’s success and ensure that the whole family can participate in a truly remarkable Husky Experience.</p>
<p>Throughout your student’s time at the UW, you can count on us to help you stay connected — to what’s happening on campus, to the wide variety of events and engagement opportunities available to UW families, and most importantly, to your student.</p>
<p>&nbsp;</p>
</div>
<div class="col-md-1">
</div>
<div class="col-md-3">

<div style="width:100%">
<h3 class="uni">About Parent &amp; Family Programs</h3>
<p>Parents and families are vital partners of the University of Washington to help our students develop into independent and responsible future leaders. The mission of Parent and Family Programs is to provide a window into the student experience at UW, actively providing opportunities for families to engage and create their own University of Washington experiences, enriching not only the lives of students but the University community at large.<br />
<a class="uni" style="font-size: 1.2em;font-weight: bold;color: #0066cc" href="meet-our-team">Meet our team</a>
</div>

	<li id="menu-item-669" class="menu-item menu-item-type-custom menu-item-object-custom menu-item-669"><a href="http://police.uw.edu/aboutus/divisions/operations/criminalinvestigations/victimadvocacy/">UWPD Victim Advocacy</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
<li id="menu-item-676" class="menu-item menu-item-type-post_type menu-item-object-page menu-item-has-children menu-item-676"><a href="https://www.washington.edu/studentlife/career-prep/">Career prep</a>
<ul class="sub-menu">
	<li id="menu-item-654" class="menu-item menu-item-type-custom menu-item-object-custom menu-item-654"><a href="http://careers.uw.edu/">Career &amp; Internship Center</a></li>
	<li id="menu-item-670" class="menu-item menu-item-type-post_type menu-item-object-page menu-item-670"><a href="https://www.washington.edu/studentlife/career-prep/work-on-campus/">Finding and maximizing campus jobs</a></li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul></div></ul></nav>      <nav class='uw-breadcrumbs' aria-label='breadcrumbs'><ul><li><a href="http://uw.edu" title="University of Washington">Home</a></li><li class="current"><a href="https://www.washington.edu/studentlife/" title="Student Life">Student Life</a><li></ul></nav>
      <div id='main_content' class="uw-body-copy" tabindex="-1">


        

<p>We&#8217;re here to help UW students make the most of their Husky Experience, bringing together the people, places and programs that support their growth, wellness and success both within and outside of the classroom &#8211; at UW and in the world beyond.</p>
<div class="box-outer">
<div class="box two box-none">
<div class="tile">
<div><img class="alignnone wp-image-292 size-half" src="https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232113/living-on-campus-375x249.jpg" alt="Residence hall on the University of Washington campus." width="375" height="249" srcset="https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232113/living-on-campus-375x249.jpg 375w, https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232113/living-on-campus-300x200.jpg 300w, https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232113/living-on-campus.jpg 600w" sizes="(max-width: 375px) 100vw, 375px" /></div>
<h2><a href="https://www.washington.edu/studentlife/living-dining/">Find your community &#8211; and a great meal  </a></h2>
<p>Want to live on campus, off campus or in Greek housing? Explore your options, and find out where to grab a bite to eat while you think about it. </p>
</div>
<div class="tile">
<div><img class="alignnone size-half wp-image-254" src="https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232225/Emmert_Portraits09_0062-1-375x250.jpg" alt="Students in paneled room." width="375" height="250" srcset="https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232225/Emmert_Portraits09_0062-1-375x250.jpg 375w, https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232225/Emmert_Portraits09_0062-1-300x200.jpg 300w, https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232225/Emmert_Portraits09_0062-1-1024x683.jpg 1024w, https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232225/Emmert_Portraits09_0062-1-750x500.jpg 750w, https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232225/Emmert_Portraits09_0062-1-1140x760.jpg 1140w" sizes="(max-width: 375px) 100vw, 375px" /></div>
<h2><a href="https://www.washington.edu/studentlife/groups-activities/">Get involved</a></h2>
<p>From registered student organizations to volunteer opportunities, recognition programs and more, the UW offers tons of rewarding and fun ways to get engaged on campus.</p>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="box-outer">
<div class="box two box-none">
<div class="tile">
<div><img class="alignnone size-half wp-image-237" src="https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232250/2A7P0011-2-375x250.jpg" alt="UW faculty member talking with a student." width="375" height="250" srcset="https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232250/2A7P0011-2-375x250.jpg 375w, https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232250/2A7P0011-2-300x200.jpg 300w, https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232250/2A7P0011-2-1024x683.jpg 1024w, https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232250/2A7P0011-2-750x500.jpg 750w, https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232250/2A7P0011-2-1140x760.jpg 1140w" sizes="(max-width: 375px) 100vw, 375px" /></div>
<h2><a href="https://www.washington.edu/studentlife/career-prep/">Prepare for your next step </a></h2>
<p>It&#8217;s never too early to start planning for internships or your future career. Discover resources and services at the Career &amp; Internship Center and within your academic department. </p>
</div>
<div class="tile">
<div><img class="alignnone wp-image-279 size-half" src="https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232144/Health-_-Wellness-375x250.jpg" alt="SStudents and visitors walking and biking around the Quad." width="375" height="250" srcset="https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232144/Health-_-Wellness-375x250.jpg 375w, https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232144/Health-_-Wellness-300x200.jpg 300w, https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232144/Health-_-Wellness-1024x683.jpg 1024w, https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232144/Health-_-Wellness-750x500.jpg 750w, https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232144/Health-_-Wellness-1140x760.jpg 1140w" sizes="(max-width: 375px) 100vw, 375px" /></div>
<h2><a href="https://www.washington.edu/studentlife/health/">Be well</a></h2>
<p>Find programs services to help you stay healthy – emotionally, mentally and physically – so you can make the most of your time at the UW. </p>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="box-outer">
<div class="box two box-none">
<div class="tile">
<div><img class="alignnone size-half wp-image-229" src="https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232316/FallCampus_32-2-375x249.jpg" alt="A crowd of students in Red Square on a sunny day at the University of Washington Seattle." width="375" height="249" srcset="https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232316/FallCampus_32-2-375x249.jpg 375w, https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232316/FallCampus_32-2-300x199.jpg 300w, https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232316/FallCampus_32-2-1024x680.jpg 1024w, https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232316/FallCampus_32-2-750x498.jpg 750w, https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/10/08232316/FallCampus_32-2-1140x757.jpg 1140w" sizes="(max-width: 375px) 100vw, 375px" /></div>
<h2><a href="https://www.washington.edu/studentlife/campus-safety/">Stay safe </a></h2>
<p>We all deserve to live, work, study and socialize in an environment that’s free of violence and harassment. Check out these services for keeping safe on and around campus.</p>
</div>
<div class="tile">
<div><img class="alignnone size-half wp-image-402" src="https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/09/08232047/uw-graduation-375x250.jpg" alt="uw graduation" width="375" height="250" srcset="https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/09/08232047/uw-graduation-375x250.jpg 375w, https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/09/08232047/uw-graduation-300x200.jpg 300w, https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/09/08232047/uw-graduation-750x500.jpg 750w, https://s3-us-west-2.amazonaws.com/uw-s3-cdn/wp-content/uploads/sites/117/2015/09/08232047/uw-graduation.jpg 960w" sizes="(max-width: 375px) 100vw, 375px" /></div>
<h2><a href="http://www.washington.edu/ceremony/">Celebrate</a></h2>
<p>UW Convocation and Commencement bookend a student&#8217;s transformative educational experience at the University.</p>
</div>
</div>
